257Non-Small Cell Lung Cancer Treatment (PDQ)Patient Version</h2>

264

265 <h3>

266General Information About Non-Small Cell Lung Cancer</h3>

267

268 <div id="_118" class="pdq-sections">

269

270 <div id="_section_118" class="pdq-sections">

271<div class="pdq-hp-patient-toggle">

272<a href="/types/lung/hp/non-small-cell-lung-treatment-pdq">

273Go to Health Professional Version</a>

274</div>

275<div class="key-points">

276<h3 id="_118_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

277Key Points</h3>

278<div id="_kp_section_118_1">

279<ul>

280<li>

281Non-small cell lung cancer is a disease in which malignant

282 (cancer) cells form in the tissues of the lung. </li>

283<li>

284There are several types of non-small cell lung cancer.</li>

285<li>

286Smoking is the major risk factor for non-small cell lung cancer.</li>

287<li>

288Signs of non-small cell lung cancer include a cough that doesn't go away and shortness of breath.</li>

289<li>

290Tests that examine the lungs are used to diagnose and stage non-small cell lung cancer.</li>

291<li>

292If lung cancer is suspected, a biopsy is done.</li>

293<li>

294Certain factors affect prognosis (chance of recovery) and treatment options.</li>

295<li>

296For most patients with non-small cell lung cancer, current

297 treatments do not cure the cancer. </li>

298</ul>

299</div>

300</div>

301<section id="_119">

302<h3 id="_120" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

303Non-small cell lung cancer is a disease in which malignant

304 (cancer) cells form in the tissues of the lung. </h3>

305<p id="_121" tabindex="-1">

306The <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270740&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270740&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

307lungs</a>

308 are a pair of cone-shaped breathing <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

309organs</a>

310 in the chest. The lungs bring <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=538149&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000538149&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

311oxygen</a>

312 into the body as you breathe in. They release <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=538147&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000538147&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

313carbon dioxide</a>

314, a waste product of the body&#8217;s <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

315cells</a>

316, as you breathe out. Each

317 lung has sections called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46188&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046188&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

318lobes</a>

319. The left lung has two

320 lobes. The right lung is

321 slightly larger and has three lobes. Two

322 tubes called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46493&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046493&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

323bronchi</a>

324 lead from the

325 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46623&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046623&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

326trachea</a>

327 (windpipe) to the right and

328 left lungs. The bronchi are sometimes also involved in <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=445043&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000445043&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

329lung cancer</a>

330. Tiny air sacs called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46209&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046209&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

331alveoli</a>

332 and small tubes called

333 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46494&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046494&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

334bronchioles</a>

335 make up the inside of

336 the lungs.<figure id="figure_292" class="image-center">

337<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/466533.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

338Enlarge</a>

339<img id="_292" alt="Respiratory system anatomy; drawing shows the right lung with the upper, middle, and lower lobes, the left lung with the upper and lower lobes, and the trachea, bronchi, lymph nodes, and diaphragm. An inset shows the bronchioles, alveoli, artery, and vein." title="Respiratory system anatomy; drawing shows the right lung with the upper, middle, and lower lobes, the left lung with the upper and lower lobes, and the trachea, bronchi, lymph nodes, and diaphragm. An inset shows the bronchioles, alveoli, artery, and vein." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/466533-750.jpg">

340<figcaption class="caption-container">

341Anatomy of the respiratory system showing the trachea, the right and left lungs and their lobes, and the bronchi. The lymph nodes and the diaphragm are also shown. Oxygen is inhaled into the lungs and passes through the alveoli (the tiny air sacs at the end of the bronchioles) and into the bloodstream (see inset), where it travels to the tissues throughout the body.</figcaption>

342</figure>

343</p>

344<p id="_276" tabindex="-1">

345A thin <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46294&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046294&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

346membrane</a>

347 called the

348 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45842&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045842&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

349pleura</a>

350 covers the outside of each lung and lines the inside wall of the chest <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=463703&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000463703&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

351cavity</a>

352. This creates a sac called the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46222&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046222&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

353pleural cavity</a>

354.

355The pleural cavity normally contains a small amount of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

356fluid</a>

357 that helps the lungs move smoothly in the chest when you breathe. </p>

358<p id="_122" tabindex="-1">

359There are two main types of lung cancer: <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45323&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045323&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

360non-small cell lung cancer</a>

361 and

362 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45327&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045327&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

363small cell lung cancer</a>

364. </p>

394<section id="_123">

395<h3 id="_124" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

396There are several types of non-small cell lung cancer.</h3>

397<p id="_125" tabindex="-1">

398Each type of non-small cell lung cancer has different kinds of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

399cancer</a>

400 cells. The cancer

401 cells of each type grow and spread in different ways. The types of non-small

402 cell lung cancer are named for the kinds of cells found in the cancer and how

403 the cells look under a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

404microscope</a>

405:</p>

406<div class="pdq-content-list">

407<ul id="_126">

408<li>

409<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46595&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046595&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

410Squamous cell

411 carcinoma</a>

412: Cancer that forms in the thin, flat cells lining the inside of the lungs. This is also called epidermoid

413 carcinoma.</li>

414<li>

415<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46316&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046316&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

416Large cell

417 carcinoma</a>

418: Cancer that may begin in several types of large cells.</li>

419<li>

420<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46216&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046216&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

421Adenocarcinoma</a>

422:

423 Cancer that begins in the cells that line the alveoli and make substances such as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46274&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046274&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

424mucus</a>

425. </li>

426</ul>

427</div>

428<p id="_278" tabindex="-1">

429Other less common types of non-small cell lung cancer are: <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476766&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476766&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

430adenosquamous carcinoma</a>

431, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476767&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476767&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

432sarcomatoid carcinoma</a>

433, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=446528&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000446528&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

434salivary gland carcinoma</a>

435, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44233&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044233&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

436carcinoid tumor</a>

437, and unclassified carcinoma.</p>

439<section id="_262">

440<h3 id="_263" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

441Smoking is the major risk factor for non-small cell lung cancer.</h3>

442<section id="_sm_CDR0000752316_1">

443<p id="_sm_CDR0000752316_5" tabindex="-1">

444Anything that increases your chance of getting a disease

445 is called a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45873&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045873&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

446risk factor</a>

447. Having a risk factor does not mean that you will get cancer; not having risk factors doesn't mean that you will not get cancer. Talk to your doctor if you think you may be at risk for lung cancer.</p>

448<p id="_sm_CDR0000752316_4" tabindex="-1">

449Risk factors for lung cancer include the following:</p>

450<div class="pdq-content-list">

451<ul id="_sm_CDR0000752316_2">

452<li>

453 Smoking <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=748148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000748148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

454cigarettes</a>

455, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=748824&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000748824&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

456pipes</a>

457, or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=748146&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000748146&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

458cigars</a>

459, now or in the past. This is the most important risk factor for lung cancer. The earlier in life a person starts smoking, the more often a person smokes, and the more years a person smokes, the greater the risk of lung cancer.</li>

460<li>

461 Being exposed to <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=538647&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000538647&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

462secondhand smoke</a>

463.</li>

464<li>

466asbestos</a>

467, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44303&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044303&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

472radiation</a>

473 from any of the following:<div class="pdq-content-list">

480 or chest.</li>

517Older age is the main risk factor for most cancers. The chance of getting cancer increases as you get older.</p>

523<h3 id="_267" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

524Signs of non-small cell lung cancer include a cough that doesn't go away and shortness of breath.</h3>

525<p id="_268" tabindex="-1">

526Sometimes lung cancer does not cause any <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

527signs</a>

529symptoms</a>

578<section id="_270">

579<h3 id="_271" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

580Tests that examine the lungs are used to diagnose and stage non-small cell lung cancer.</h3>

581<p id="_272" tabindex="-1">

582Tests and procedures to <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

583diagnose</a>

584 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

585stage</a>

586 non-small cell lung cancer are often done at the same time. Some of the following tests and procedures may be used:</p>

587<div class="pdq-content-list">

588<ul id="_273">

589<li>

590

591

592<strong>

593<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270871&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270871&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

594Physical exam</a>

595 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=798522&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000798522&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

596health history</a>

597</strong>

598: An exam of the body to check general signs of health, including checking for signs of disease, such as lumps or anything else that seems unusual. A history of the patient&#8217;s health habits, including smoking, and past jobs, illnesses, and treatments will also be taken.</li>

599<li>

600<strong>

601<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46590&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046590&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

602Laboratory tests</a>

603</strong>

604: Medical procedures that test samples of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

605tissue</a>

606, blood, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46642&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046642&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

607urine</a>

608, or other substances in the body. These tests help to diagnose disease, plan and check treatment, or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=454803&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000454803&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

609monitor</a>

610 the disease over time.</li>

611<li>

612<strong>

613Chest x-ray</strong>

614: An <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

615x-ray</a>

616 of the organs and bones inside the chest. An x-ray is a type of energy beam that can go through the body and onto film, making a picture of areas inside the body.

617<figure id="figure_293" class="image-center">

618<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/428438.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

619Enlarge</a>

X-rays pass through the patient onto film." title="Chest x-ray; drawing shows the patient standing with her back to the x-ray machine. X-rays are used to take pictures of organs and bones of the chest. X-rays pass through the patient onto film." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/428438-750.jpg">

621<figcaption class="caption-container">

622X-ray of the chest. X-rays are used to take pictures of organs and bones of the chest. X-rays pass through the patient onto film. </figcaption>

623</figure>

624</li>

625<li>

626<strong>

627<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

628CT scan</a>

629 (CAT scan)</strong>

630: A procedure that makes a series of detailed pictures of areas inside the body, such as the chest, taken from different angles. The pictures are made by a computer linked to an x-ray machine. A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=409764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000409764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

631dye</a>

632 may be <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

633injected</a>

634 into a vein or swallowed to help the organs or tissues show up more clearly. This procedure is also called computed tomography, computerized tomography, or computerized axial tomography.

635</li>

636<li>

637<strong>

638<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=335080&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000335080&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

639Sputum cytology</a>

640</strong>

641: A procedure in which a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

642pathologist</a>

643 views a sample of sputum (mucus coughed up from the lungs) under a microscope, to check for cancer cells.</li>

644<li>

645<strong>

646<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46612&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046612&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

647Thoracentesis</a>

648</strong>

649: The removal of fluid from the space between the lining of the chest and the lung, using a needle. A pathologist views the fluid under a microscope to look for cancer cells.</li>

650</ul>

651</div>

652</section>

653<section id="_476">

654<h3 id="_477" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

655If lung cancer is suspected, a biopsy is done.</h3>

656<p id="_478" tabindex="-1">

657One of the following types of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45164&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045164&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

658biopsies</a>

659 is usually used: </p>

660<div class="pdq-content-list">

661<ul id="_479">

662<li>

663<strong>

664<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45691&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045691&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

665Fine-needle aspiration (FNA) biopsy</a>

666 of the lung</strong>

667: The removal of tissue or fluid from the lung using a thin needle. A CT scan, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46157&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046157&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

668ultrasound</a>

669, or other <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45720&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045720&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

670imaging procedure</a>

671 is used to locate the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44636&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044636&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

672abnormal</a>

673 tissue or fluid in the lung. A small <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46353&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046353&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

674incision</a>

675 may be made in the skin where the biopsy needle is inserted into the abnormal tissue or fluid. A sample is removed with the needle and sent to the laboratory. A pathologist then views the sample under a microscope to look for cancer cells. A chest x-ray is done after the procedure to make sure no air is leaking from the lung into the chest.<figure id="figure_309" class="image-center">

676<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/531057.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

677Enlarge</a>

678<img id="_309" alt="Fine-needle aspiration biopsy of the lung; drawing shows a patient lying on a table that slides through the computed tomography (CT) machine with an x-ray picture of a cross-section of the lung on a monitor above the patient. Drawing also shows a doctor using the x-ray picture to help place the biopsy needle through the chest wall and into the area of abnormal lung tissue. Inset shows a side view of the chest cavity and lungs with the biopsy needle inserted into the area of abnormal tissue." title="Fine-needle aspiration biopsy of the lung; drawing shows a patient lying on a table that slides through the computed tomography (CT) machine with an x-ray picture of a cross-section of the lung on a monitor above the patient. Inset shows a side view of the chest cavity and lungs with the biopsy needle inserted into the area of abnormal tissue." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/531057-750.jpg">

679<figcaption class="caption-container">

680Fine-needle aspiration biopsy of the lung. The patient lies on a table that slides through the computed tomography (CT) machine, which takes x-ray pictures of the inside of the body. The x-ray pictures help the doctor see where the abnormal tissue is in the lung. A biopsy needle is inserted through the chest wall and into the area of abnormal lung tissue. A small piece of tissue is removed through the needle and checked under the microscope for signs of cancer. </figcaption>

681</figure>

682<p id="_480" tabindex="-1">

683An <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46602&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046602&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

684endoscopic ultrasound</a>

685 (EUS) is a type of ultrasound that may be used to guide an FNA biopsy of the lung, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45762&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045762&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

686lymph nodes</a>

687, or other areas. EUS is a procedure in which an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46428&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046428&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

688endoscope</a>

689 is inserted into the body. An endoscope is a thin, tube-like instrument with a light and a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=572035&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000572035&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

690lens</a>

691 for viewing. A probe at the end of the endoscope is used to bounce high-energy sound waves (ultrasound) off internal tissues or organs and make echoes. The echoes form a picture of body tissues called a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46587&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046587&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

692sonogram</a>

693.</p>

694<figure id="figure_315" class="image-center">

695<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/466552.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

696Enlarge</a>

697<img id="_315" alt="Endoscopic ultrasound-guided fine-needle aspiration biopsy; drawing shows an endoscope with an ultrasound probe and biopsy needle inserted through the mouth and into the esophagus. Also shown are the lymph nodes near the esophagus and cancer in one lung. 698<figcaption class="caption-container">

699Endoscopic ultrasound-guided fine-needle aspiration biopsy. An endoscope that has an ultrasound probe and a biopsy needle is inserted through the mouth and into the esophagus. 700</figure>

701</li>

702<li>

703<strong>

704<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45628&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045628&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

705Bronchoscopy</a>

706</strong>

707: A procedure to look inside the trachea and large airways in the lung for abnormal areas. A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46496&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046496&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

708bronchoscope</a>

709 is inserted through the nose or mouth into the trachea and lungs. A bronchoscope is a thin, tube-like instrument with a light and a lens for viewing. It may also have a tool to remove tissue samples, which are checked under a microscope for signs of cancer.<figure id="figure_295" class="image-center">

710<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/435997.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

715</figure>

716</li>

717<li>

718<strong>

719<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46119&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046119&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

720Thoracoscopy</a>

721</strong>

722: A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

723surgical</a>

724 procedure to look at the organs inside the chest to check for abnormal areas. An incision (cut) is made between two ribs, and a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476929&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476929&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

725thoracoscope</a>

726 is inserted into the chest. A thoracoscope is a thin, tube-like instrument with a light and a lens for viewing. It may also have a tool to remove tissue or lymph node samples, which are checked under a microscope for signs of cancer. In some cases, this procedure is used to remove part of the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46408&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046408&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

727esophagus</a>

728 or lung. If certain tissues, organs, or lymph nodes can&#8217;t be reached, a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45926&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045926&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

729thoracotomy</a>

730 may be done. In this procedure, a larger incision is made between the ribs and the chest is opened. </li>

731<li>

732<strong>

733<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46287&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046287&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

734Mediastinoscopy</a>

735</strong>

736: A surgical procedure to look at the organs, tissues, and lymph nodes between the lungs for abnormal areas. An incision (cut) is made at the top of the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=549425&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000549425&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

737breastbone</a>

738 and a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=514453&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000514453&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

739mediastinoscope</a>

740 is inserted into the chest. A mediastinoscope is a thin, tube-like instrument with a light and a lens for viewing. It may also have a tool to remove tissue or lymph node samples, which are checked under a microscope for signs of cancer.<figure id="figure_296" class="image-center">

756</li>

757<li>

758<strong>

760Anterior

761 mediastinotomy</a>

762</strong>

763: A surgical procedure to look at the organs and tissues between the lungs and between the breastbone and heart for abnormal areas. An incision (cut) is made next to the breastbone and a mediastinoscope is inserted into the chest. A mediastinoscope is a thin, tube-like instrument with a light and a lens for viewing. It may also have a tool to remove tissue or lymph node samples, which are checked under a microscope for signs of cancer. This is also called the Chamberlain procedure.</li>

764<li>

765<strong>

766<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=793499&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000793499&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

767Lymph node biopsy</a>

768</strong>

769: The removal of all or part of a lymph node. A pathologist views the lymph node tissue under a microscope to check for cancer cells.</li>

772<p id="_481" tabindex="-1">

773One or more of the following laboratory tests may be done to study the tissue samples:</p>

774<div class="pdq-content-list">

775<ul id="_482">

776<li>

777<strong>

778<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=766166&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000766166&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

779Molecular test</a>

780</strong>

781: A laboratory test to check for certain <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45693&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045693&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

782genes</a>

783, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46092&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046092&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

784proteins</a>

785, or other <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45065&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045065&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

786molecules</a>

787 in a sample of tissue, blood, or other body fluid. Molecular tests check for certain gene or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46470&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046470&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

788chromosome</a>

789 changes that occur in non-small cell lung cancer.</li>

790<li>

791<strong>

792<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=653117&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000653117&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

793Immunohistochemistry</a>

794</strong>

795: A laboratory test that uses <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44918&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044918&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

796antibodies</a>

797 to check for certain <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46086&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046086&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

798antigens</a>

799 (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45776&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045776&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

800markers</a>

801) in a sample of a patient&#8217;s tissue. The antibodies are usually linked to an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46081&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046081&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

802enzyme</a>

803 or a fluorescent dye. After the antibodies bind to a specific antigen in the tissue sample, the enzyme or dye is activated, and the antigen can then be seen under a microscope. This type of test is used to help diagnose cancer and to help tell one type of cancer from another type of cancer.</li>

804</ul>

807<section id="_127">

808<h3 id="_128" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

809Certain factors affect prognosis (chance of recovery) and treatment options.</h3>

810<p id="_244" tabindex="-1">

811The <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45849&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045849&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

812prognosis</a>

813 and treatment options depend on the following:</p>

814<div class="pdq-content-list">

815<ul id="_243">

816<li>

817The stage of the cancer (the size of the tumor and whether it is

818 in the lung only or has spread to other places in the body).</li>

819<li>

820The type of lung

821 cancer.</li>

822<li>

823Whether the cancer has <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46063&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046063&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

824mutations</a>

825 (changes) in certain genes, such as the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=796875&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000796875&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

826epidermal growth factor receptor (EGFR) gene</a>

827 or the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=721259&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000721259&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

828anaplastic lymphoma kinase (ALK) gene</a>

829.</li>

830<li>

831Whether there are signs and symptoms such as coughing or trouble breathing.</li>

832<li>

833The patient&#8217;s general health. </li>

834</ul>

835</div>

836</section>

837<section id="_130">

838<h3 id="_131" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

839For most patients with non-small cell lung cancer, current

840 treatments do not cure the cancer. </h3>

841<p id="_132" tabindex="-1">

842If lung cancer is found, taking part in one of the many <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

843clinical

844 trials</a>

845 being done to improve treatment should be considered. Clinical trials

846 are taking place in most parts of the country for patients with all stages of

847 non-small cell lung cancer. Information about ongoing clinical trials is

848 available from the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials">

849NCI website</a>

850.</p>

851</section>

852</div>

853

854 </div>

858 <h3>

859Stages of Non-Small Cell Lung Cancer</h3>

860

861 <div id="_134" class="pdq-sections">

862

863 <div id="_section_134" class="pdq-sections">

864<div class="key-points">

865<h3 id="_134_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

866Key Points</h3>

867<div id="_kp_section_134_2">

868<ul>

869<li>

870After lung cancer has been diagnosed, tests are done to

871 find out if cancer cells have spread within the lungs or to other parts of the

872 body. </li>

873<li>

874There are three ways that cancer spreads in the body.</li>

875<li>

876Cancer may spread from where it began to other parts of the body.</li>

877<li>

878The following stages are used for non-small cell lung

879 cancer:<ul>

880<li>

881Occult (hidden) stage</li>

882<li>

883Stage 0</li>

884<li>

885Stage I</li>

886<li>

887Stage II</li>

888<li>

889Stage III</li>

890<li>

891Stage IV</li>

892</ul>

893</li>

894<li>

895Non-small cell

896 lung cancer can recur

897 (come back) after it has been treated. </li>

898</ul>

899</div>

901<section id="_135">

902<h3 id="_136" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

903After lung cancer has been diagnosed, tests are done to

904 find out if cancer cells have spread within the lungs or to other parts of the

905 body. </h3>

906<p id="_137" tabindex="-1">

907The process used to find out if <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

908cancer</a>

909 has spread within the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270740&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270740&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

910lungs</a>

911 or to other parts

912 of the body is called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46597&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046597&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

913staging</a>

914. The information gathered from the

915 staging process determines the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

916stage</a>

917 of the disease. It is

918 important to know the stage in order to plan treatment. Some of the tests used to <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

919diagnose</a>

920 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45323&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045323&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

921non-small cell lung cancer</a>

922 are also used to stage the disease. For more information, see the <a href="/types/lung/patient/non-small-cell-lung-treatment-pdq#_270">

923General Information</a>

924 section. </p>

925<p id="_462" tabindex="-1">

926Other tests and procedures

927 that may be used in the staging process include the following:</p>

928<div class="pdq-content-list">

929<ul id="_138">

930<li>

931<strong>

932<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45788&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045788&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

933MRI</a>

934 (magnetic resonance imaging)</strong>

935: A procedure that uses a magnet, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651209&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651209&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

936radio waves</a>

937, and a computer to make a series of detailed pictures of areas inside the body, such as the brain. This procedure is also called nuclear magnetic resonance imaging (NMRI).</li>

938<li>

939<strong>

940<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

941CT scan</a>

942 (CAT scan)</strong>

943: A procedure that makes a series of detailed pictures of areas inside the body, such as the brain, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45070&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045070&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

944abdomen</a>

945, and lymph nodes, taken from different angles. The pictures are made by a computer linked to an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

946x-ray</a>

947 machine. A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=409764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000409764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

948dye</a>

949 may be <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

950injected</a>

951 into a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

952vein</a>

953 or swallowed to help the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

954organs</a>

958<li>

962 (positron emission tomography scan)</strong>

964malignant</a>

965 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

966tumor</a>

967 cells in the body. A small amount of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46550&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046550&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

968radioactive</a>

969 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

970glucose</a>

971 (sugar) is injected into a vein. The PET <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=386220&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000386220&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

972scanner</a>

973 rotates around the body and makes a picture of where glucose is being used in the body. Malignant tumor cells show up brighter in the picture because they are more active and take up more glucose than normal cells do.<figure id="figure_294" class="image-center">

974<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/466545.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

977<figcaption class="caption-container">

978PET (positron emission tomography) scan. The patient lies on a table that slides through the PET machine. The head rest and white strap help the patient lie still. A small amount of radioactive glucose (sugar) is injected into the patient's vein, and a scanner makes a picture of where the glucose is being used in the body. Cancer cells show up brighter in the picture because they take up more glucose than normal cells do.

979</figcaption>

980</figure>

981</li>

982<li>

983<strong>

985Bone scan</a>

986</strong>

987: A procedure to check if there are rapidly dividing <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

988cells</a>

989, such as cancer cells, in the bone. A very small amount of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46550&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046550&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

990radioactive</a>

991 material is <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

992injected</a>

993 into a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

994vein</a>

995 and travels through the bloodstream. The radioactive material collects in the bones with cancer and is detected by a scanner.</li>

996<li>

997<strong>

998<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=658018&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000658018&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

999Pulmonary function test</a>

1000 (PFT)</strong>

1001: A test to see how well the lungs are working. It measures how much air the lungs can hold and how quickly air moves into and out of the lungs. It also measures how much <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=538149&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000538149&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1002oxygen</a>

1003 is used and how much <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=538147&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000538147&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1004carbon dioxide</a>

1005 is given off during breathing. This is also called lung function test.</li>

1006<li>

1007<strong>

1008<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=669655&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000669655&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1010</strong>

1011: The removal of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45622&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045622&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1015, and a small piece of bone by inserting a hollow needle into the hipbone or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=549425&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000549425&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1016breastbone</a>

A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1018pathologist</a>

1019 views the bone marrow, blood, and bone under a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1020microscope</a>

1021 to look for <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1022signs</a>

1023 of cancer.</li>

1027<section id="_317">

1028<h3 id="_318" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1029There are three ways that cancer spreads in the body.</h3>

1030<p id="_317_md_69" tabindex="-1">

1031Cancer can spread through <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1032tissue</a>

1033, the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1034lymph system</a>

1035, and the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1036blood</a>

1037:</p>

1038<div class="pdq-content-list">

1039<ul id="_317_md_70">

1040<li>

1041Tissue. The cancer spreads from where it began by growing into nearby areas.

1042</li>

1043<li>

1044Lymph system. The cancer spreads from where it began by getting into the lymph system. The cancer travels through the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1045lymph vessels</a>

1046 to other parts of the body.

1047</li>

1048<li>

1049Blood. The cancer spreads from where it began by getting into the blood. The cancer travels through the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45020&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045020&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1050blood vessels</a>

1051 to other parts of the body.

1052</li>

1053</ul>

1054</div>

1055</section>

1056<section id="_432">

1057<h3 id="_433" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1058Cancer may spread from where it began to other parts of the body.</h3>

1059<p id="_432_md_66" tabindex="-1">

1060When cancer spreads to another part of the body, it is called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46710&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046710&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1061metastasis</a>

1062. Cancer <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1063cells</a>

1064 break away from where they began (the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45847&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045847&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1065primary tumor</a>

1066) and travel through the lymph system or blood.</p>

1067<div class="pdq-content-list">

1068<ul id="_432_md_67">

1069<li>

1070Lymph system. The cancer gets into the lymph system, travels through the lymph vessels, and forms a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1071tumor</a>

1072 (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44058&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044058&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1073metastatic</a>

1074 tumor) in another part of the body.</li>

1075<li>

1076Blood. The cancer gets into the blood, travels through the blood vessels, and forms a tumor (metastatic tumor) in another part of the body.</li>

1077</ul>

1078</div>

1079<p id="_434" tabindex="-1">

1080The metastatic tumor is the same type of cancer as the primary tumor. For example, if non-small cell lung cancer spreads to the brain, the cancer cells in the brain are actually <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=445043&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000445043&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1081lung cancer</a>

1082 cells. The disease is metastatic lung cancer, not brain cancer.</p>

1083<div data-embed-button="media_entity_embed" data-entity-embed-display="view_mode:media.video_display_medium_no_title" data-entity-type="media" data-caption="" class="embedded-entity align-center">

1084<figure class="video">

1085<div id="ytplayer-fQwar_-QdiQ" class="flex-video widescreen" data-video-url="https://www.youtube.com/embed/fQwar_-QdiQ?feature=oembed&amp;autoplay=1" data-video-title="metastasis: how cancer spreads">

1086<iframe width="560" height="315" src="https://www.youtube-nocookie.com/embed/fQwar_-QdiQ?rel=0" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" title="metastasis: how cancer spreads" alt="metastasis: how cancer spreads" allowfullscreen="">

1087</iframe>

1088</div>

1089<figcaption class="caption-container">

1090Many cancer deaths are caused when cancer moves from the original tumor and spreads to other tissues and organs. This is called metastatic cancer. This animation shows how cancer cells travel from the place in the body where they first formed to other parts of the body.</figcaption>

1091</figure>

1092</div>

1093</section>

1094<section id="_140">

1095<h3 id="_141" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1096The following stages are used for non-small cell lung

1097 cancer:</h3>

1098<section id="_142">

1099<h4 id="_143" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1100Occult (hidden) stage</h4>

1101<p id="_483" tabindex="-1">

1338<section id="_500">

1339<h4 id="_501" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1340Stage III</h4>

1341<p id="_502" tabindex="-1">

1342Stage III is divided into stages IIIA, IIIB, and IIIC. </p>

1343<div class="pdq-content-list">

1344<ul id="_503">

1345<li>

1346<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45367&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045367&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1347Stage IIIA</a>

1348: <figure id="figure_539" class="image-center">

1349<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/521911.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1350Enlarge</a>

1351<img id="_539" alt="Stage IIIA lung cancer (1); drawing shows a primary tumor (5 cm or smaller) in the left lung (top inset) and cancer in lymph nodes around the trachea. Also shown is cancer that has spread to (a) the left main bronchus and (b) the membrane covering the lung (bottom inset). Also shown is (c) part or all of the lung has collapsed or has pneumonitis (inflammation). The carina, pleura, and a rib (bottom inset) are also shown." title="Stage IIIA lung cancer (1); drawing shows a primary tumor (5 cm or smaller) in the left lung (top inset) and cancer in lymph nodes around the trachea. Also shown is cancer that has spread to (a) the left main bronchus and (b) the membrane covering the lung (bottom inset). Also shown is (c) part or all of the lung has collapsed or has pneumonitis (inflammation). The carina, pleura, and a rib (bottom inset) are also shown." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/521911-750.jpg">

1352<figcaption class="caption-container">

1353Stage IIIA lung cancer (1). The tumor is 5 centimeters or smaller and cancer has spread to lymph nodes on the same side of the chest as the primary tumor. The lymph nodes with cancer are around the trachea or aorta (not shown), or where the trachea divides into the bronchi. Also, one or more of the following may be found: (a) cancer has spread to the main bronchus, but has not spread to the carina; and/or (b) cancer has spread to the inner membrane that covers the lung; and/or (c) part of the lung or the whole lung has collapsed or has pneumonitis (inflammation of the lung).</figcaption>

1354</figure>

1355<p id="_547" tabindex="-1">

1356The <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1357tumor</a>

1358 is 5 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=354457&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000354457&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1359centimeters</a>

1360 or smaller and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1361cancer</a>

1629<p id="_523" tabindex="-1">

1641Stage IVA lung cancer. The tumor may be any size and cancer may have spread to the lymph nodes. 1712Treatment Option Overview</h3>

1716 <div id="_section_164" class="pdq-sections">

1717<div class="key-points">

1718<h3 id="_164_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

1719Key Points</h3>

1720<div id="_kp_section_164_3">

1721<ul>

1722<li>

1723There are different types of treatment for patients with non-small cell lung cancer.</li>

1724<li>

1725The following types of treatment are used:<ul>

1726<li>

1727Surgery </li>

1728<li>

1729Radiation therapy </li>

1730<li>

1731Chemotherapy </li>

1732<li>

1733Targeted therapy</li>

1734<li>

1735Immunotherapy</li>

1736<li>

1737Laser therapy</li>

1738<li>

1739Photodynamic therapy (PDT)</li>

1740<li>

1741Cryosurgery</li>

1742<li>

1743Electrocautery</li>

1744</ul>

1745</li>

1746<li>

1747New types of treatment are being tested in

1748 clinical trials. <ul>

1749<li>

1750Radiosensitizers</li>

1751<li>

1752New combinations</li>

1753</ul>

1754</li>

1755<li>

1756Treatment for non-small cell lung cancer may cause side effects.</li>

1757<li>

1758Patients may want to think about taking part in a clinical trial.</li>

1759<li>

1760Patients can enter clinical trials before, during, or after starting their cancer treatment.</li>

1761<li>

1762Follow-up tests may be needed.</li>

1763</ul>

1764</div>

1766<section id="_284">

1767<h3 id="_285" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1768There are different types of treatment for patients with non-small cell lung cancer.</h3>

1769<p id="_286" tabindex="-1">

1770Different types of treatments are available for patients with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45323&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045323&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1771non-small cell lung cancer</a>

1772. Some treatments are <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1773standard</a>

1774 (the currently used treatment), and some are being tested in <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1775clinical trials</a>

1776. A treatment clinical trial is a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651211&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651211&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1777research study</a>

1778 meant to help improve current treatments or obtain information on new treatments for patients with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1779cancer</a>

1780. When clinical trials show that a new treatment is better than the standard treatment, the new treatment may become the standard treatment. Patients may want to think about taking part in a clinical trial. Some clinical trials are open only to patients who have not started treatment.</p>

1864<section id="_186">

1865<h4 id="_187" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1866Radiation therapy </h4>

1867<p id="_240" tabindex="-1">

1868Radiation therapy is a cancer treatment that uses high-energy <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1869x-rays</a>

1870 or other types of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1871radiation</a>

1872 to kill cancer cells or keep them from growing. There are two types of radiation therapy: </p>

1891<p id="_443" tabindex="-1">

1892<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=386233&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000386233&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1893Stereotactic body radiation therapy</a>

1894 is a type of external radiation therapy. Special equipment is used to place the patient in the same position for each radiation treatment. Once a day for several days, a radiation machine aims a larger than usual <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44664&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044664&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1895dose</a>

1896 of radiation directly at the tumor. By having the patient in the same position for each treatment, there is less damage to nearby healthy tissue. This procedure is also called stereotactic external-beam radiation therapy and stereotaxic radiation therapy.</p>

1897<p id="_242" tabindex="-1">

1898<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46701&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046701&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1899Stereotactic radiosurgery</a>

1900 is a type of external radiation therapy used to treat lung cancer that has spread to the brain. A rigid head frame is attached to the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=763008&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000763008&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1901skull</a>

1902 to keep the head still during the radiation treatment. A machine aims a single large dose of radiation directly at the tumor in the brain. This procedure does not involve surgery. It is also called stereotaxic radiosurgery, radiosurgery, and radiation surgery.</p>

1903<p id="_450" tabindex="-1">

1904For tumors in the airways, radiation is given directly to the tumor through an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46428&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046428&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1905endoscope</a>

1906.</p>

1907<p id="_245" tabindex="-1">

1908 The way the radiation therapy is given depends on the type and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1910 of the cancer being treated.

1911It also depends on where the cancer is found. External and internal radiation therapy are used to treat non-small cell lung cancer.</p>
